#1 cloud1 — Learn about the incredible power of praying for everyone

EN Learn about the incredible power of praying for everyone! \ud83d\ude4f When you daven (pray) to Hashem for blessings, health, and parnassa (livelihood) or for anything good for all of Am Yisrael (the Jewish people) \u2014 not just for yourself \u2014 the Sages teach that your prayer is more likely to be answered! It\u2019s like a spiritual win-win: you help yourself by helping everyone else. Plus, who doesn't want to live in a world where no one is stressed? So next time you need some blessings, broaden your scope and pray for the whole community!
HE \u05d2\u05dc\u05d5 \u05d0\u05ea \u05db\u05d5\u05d7 \u05d4\u05ea\u05e4\u05d9\u05dc\u05d4 \u05dc\u05db\u05d5\u05dc\u05dd! \ud83d\ude4f \u05db\u05e9\u05d0\u05ea\u05dd \u05de\u05ea\u05e4\u05dc\u05dc\u05d9\u05dd \u05dc\u05d4' \u05e2\u05dc \u05d1\u05e8\u05db\u05d5\u05ea, \u05d1\u05e8\u05d9\u05d0\u05d5\u05ea, \u05e4\u05e8\u05e0\u05e1\u05d4, \u05d0\u05d5 \u05e2\u05dc \u05db\u05dc \u05d3\u05d1\u05e8 \u05d8\u05d5\u05d1 \u05e2\u05d1\u05d5\u05e8 \u05db\u05dc \u05e2\u05dd \u05d9\u05e9\u05e8\u05d0\u05dc \u2014 \u05d5\u05dc\u05d0 \u05e8\u05e7 \u05e2\u05d1\u05d5\u05e8 \u05e2\u05e6\u05de\u05db\u05dd \u2014 \u05d4\u05d7\u05db\u05de\u05d9\u05dd \u05de\u05dc\u05de\u05d3\u05d9\u05dd \u05e9\u05d4\u05ea\u05e4\u05d9\u05dc\u05d4 \u05e9\u05dc\u05db\u05dd \u05e1\u05d1\u05d9\u05e8 \u05d9\u05d5\u05ea\u05e8 \u05e9\u05ea\u05d9\u05e2\u05e0\u05d4! \u05d6\u05d4 \u05db\u05de\u05d5 win-win \u05e8\u05d5\u05d7\u05e0\u05d9: \u05d0\u05ea\u05dd \u05e2\u05d5\u05d6\u05e8\u05d9\u05dd \u05dc\u05e2\u05e6\u05de\u05db\u05dd \u05d1\u05d6\u05de\u05df \u05e9\u05d0\u05ea\u05dd \u05e2\u05d5\u05d6\u05e8\u05d9\u05dd \u05dc\u05db\u05d5\u05dc\u05dd. \u05d5\u05de\u05d9 \u05dc\u05d0 \u05d4\u05d9\u05d4 \u05e8\u05d5\u05e6\u05d4 \u05dc\u05d7\u05d9\u05d5\u05ea \u05d1\u05e2\u05d5\u05dc\u05dd \u05e9\u05d1\u05d5 \u05d0\u05e3 \u05d0\u05d7\u05d3 \u05dc\u05d0 \u05dc\u05d7\u05d5\u05e5? \u05d0\u05d6 \u05d1\u05e4\u05e2\u05dd \u05d4\u05d1\u05d0\u05d4 \u05e9\u05d0\u05ea\u05dd \u05e6\u05e8\u05d9\u05db\u05d9\u05dd \u05d1\u05e8\u05db\u05d5\u05ea, \u05d4\u05e8\u05d7\u05d9\u05d1\u05d5 \u05d0\u05ea \u05d0\u05d5\u05e4\u05e7 \u05d4\u05ea\u05e4\u05d9\u05dc\u05d4 \u05d5\u05ea\u05ea\u05e4\u05dc\u05dc\u05d5 \u05e2\u05dc \u05db\u05dc \u05d4\u05e7\u05d4\u05d9\u05dc\u05d4!
ES \u00a1Descubre el incre\u00edble poder de orar por todos! \ud83d\ude4f Cuando te diriges a Hashem en tefil\u00e1 (oraci\u00f3n) pidiendo bendiciones, salud, parnas\u00e1 (sustento) o cualquier cosa buena para todo el pueblo de Israel (Am Israel) \u2014y no solo para ti\u2014 los Sabios ense\u00f1an que tu oraci\u00f3n tiene m\u00e1s probabilidades de ser escuchada. Es como un win-win espiritual: te ayudas a ti mismo al ayudar a todos. Adem\u00e1s, \u00bfqui\u00e9n no querr\u00eda vivir en un mundo donde nadie est\u00e1 estresado? #2 cloud2 — Discover a powerful prayer hack: persistent davening

EN Discover a powerful prayer hack: persistent davening! \ud83d\udde3\ufe0f Ever feel like your prayers aren't getting through? The Sages teach us the importance of persistent prayer. While there's no magic number like '20 times in a row,' the core idea is to truly pour out your heart and not give up. Think of it like a child asking a parent repeatedly for something they really need! Before you even ask for your desires, the kabbalists teach a powerful sequence: (1) Praise Hashem for His greatness, (2) Thank Him for all the blessings you already have. This helps open the 'gates of prayer' and puts you in a mindset of gratitude and trust. Keep davening with faith, and never despair! Source: Based on various rabbinic teachings on tefillah (prayer).
HE \u05d2\u05dc\u05d5 \u05d8\u05d9\u05e4 \u05ea\u05e4\u05d9\u05dc\u05d4 \u05e2\u05d5\u05e6\u05de\u05ea\u05d9: \u05d4\u05ea\u05de\u05d3\u05d4 \u05d1\u05ea\u05e4\u05d9\u05dc\u05d4! \ud83d\udde3\ufe0f \u05d0\u05d9 \u05e4\u05e2\u05dd \u05d4\u05e8\u05d2\u05e9\u05ea\u05dd \u05e9\u05d4\u05ea\u05e4\u05d9\u05dc\u05d5\u05ea \u05e9\u05dc\u05db\u05dd \u05dc\u05d0 \u05de\u05d2\u05d9\u05e2\u05d5\u05ea \u05dc\u05d9\u05e2\u05d3? \u05d4\u05d7\u05db\u05de\u05d9\u05dd \u05de\u05dc\u05de\u05d3\u05d9\u05dd \u05e2\u05dc \u05d7\u05e9\u05d9\u05d1\u05d5\u05ea \u05d4\u05ea\u05de\u05d3\u05d4 \u05d1\u05ea\u05e4\u05d9\u05dc\u05d4. \u05d0\u05d9\u05df \u05de\u05e1\u05e4\u05e8 \u05e7\u05e1\u05dd \u05db\u05de\u05d5 \"20 \u05e4\u05e2\u05de\u05d9\u05dd \u05d1\u05e8\u05e6\u05e3\", \u05d0\u05d1\u05dc \u05d4\u05e8\u05e2\u05d9\u05d5\u05df \u05d4\u05de\u05e8\u05db\u05d6\u05d9 \u05d4\u05d5\u05d0 \u05dc\u05e9\u05e4\u05d5\u05da \u05d0\u05ea \u05dc\u05d1\u05db\u05dd \u05d1\u05d0\u05de\u05ea \u05d5\u05dc\u05d0 \u05dc\u05d5\u05d5\u05ea\u05e8. \u05ea\u05d7\u05e9\u05d1\u05d5 \u05e2\u05dc \u05d9\u05dc\u05d3 \u05e9\u05de\u05d1\u05e7\u05e9 \u05de\u05d4\u05d5\u05e8\u05d4 \u05e9\u05d5\u05d1 \u05d5\u05e9\u05d5\u05d1 \u05de\u05e9\u05d4\u05d5 \u05e9\u05d4\u05d5\u05d0 \u05d1\u05d0\u05de\u05ea \u05e6\u05e8\u05d9\u05da! \u05dc\u05e4\u05e0\u05d9 \u05e9\u05d0\u05ea\u05dd \u05de\u05d1\u05e7\u05e9\u05d9\u05dd \u05d0\u05ea \u05de\u05d4 \u05e9\u05d0\u05ea\u05dd \u05d7\u05e4\u05e6\u05d9\u05dd \u05d1\u05d5, \u05d1\u05de\u05e1\u05d5\u05e8\u05ea \u05d4\u05e7\u05d1\u05dc\u05d4 \u05de\u05dc\u05de\u05d3\u05d9\u05dd \u05e8\u05e6\u05e3 \u05e2\u05d5\u05e6\u05de\u05ea\u05d9: (1) \u05e9\u05d1\u05d7\u05d5 \u05d0\u05ea \u05d4' \u05e2\u05dc \u05d2\u05d3\u05dc\u05d5\u05ea\u05d5, (2) \u05d4\u05d5\u05d3\u05d5 \u05dc\u05d5 \u05e2\u05dc \u05db\u05dc \u05d4\u05d1\u05e8\u05db\u05d5\u05ea \u05e9\u05db\u05d1\u05e8 \u05d9\u05e9 \u05dc\u05db\u05dd. \u05d6\u05d4 \u05e2\u05d5\u05d6\u05e8 \u05dc\u05e4\u05ea\u05d5\u05d7 \u05d0\u05ea \"\u05e9\u05e2\u05e8\u05d9 \u05d4\u05ea\u05e4\u05d9\u05dc\u05d4\" \u05d5\u05de\u05db\u05e0\u05d9\u05e1 \u05d0\u05ea\u05db\u05dd \u05dc\u05de\u05e6\u05d1 \u05e9\u05dc \u05d4\u05db\u05e8\u05ea \u05ea\u05d5\u05d3\u05d4 \u05d5\u05d0\u05de\u05d5\u05df. \u05d4\u05de\u05e9\u05d9\u05db\u05d5 \u05dc\u05d4\u05ea\u05e4\u05dc\u05dc \u05d1\u05d0\u05de\u05d5\u05e0\u05d4, \u05d5\u05d0\u05dc \u05ea\u05ea\u05d9\u05d9\u05d0\u05e9\u05d5 \u05dc\u05e2\u05d5\u05dc\u05dd! \u05de\u05e7\u05d5\u05e8: \u05de\u05d1\u05d5\u05e1\u05e1 \u05e2\u05dc \u05ea\u05d5\u05e8\u05d5\u05ea \u05d7\u05d6\"\u05dc \u05e9\u05d5\u05e0\u05d5\u05ea \u05d1\u05e0\u05d5\u05e9\u05d0 \u05ea\u05e4\u05d9\u05dc\u05d4.
ES Descubre un truco poderoso de oraci\u00f3n: \u00a1tefil\u00e1 persistente! \ud83d\udde3\ufe0f \u00bfAlguna vez sientes que tus oraciones no llegan? Los Sabios ense\u00f1an la importancia de la oraci\u00f3n persistente. No hay un n\u00famero m\u00e1gico como \"20 veces seguidas\", pero la idea central es derramar el coraz\u00f3n de verdad y no rendirse. \u00a1Piensa en un ni\u00f1o que le pide algo a un padre una y otra vez porque realmente lo necesita! Antes de pedir tus deseos, los cabalistas ense\u00f1an una secuencia poderosa: (1) alaba a Hashem por Su grandeza, (2) agrad\u00e9cele por todas las bendiciones que ya tienes. Esto ayuda a abrir las \"puertas de la oraci\u00f3n\" y te pone en un estado de gratitud y confianza. Sigue orando con fe y nunca te desesperes. Fuente: Basado en diversas ense\u00f1anzas rab\u00ednicas sobre tefil\u00e1.
FR D\u00e9couvrez un puissant secret de pri\u00e8re : la pers\u00e9v\u00e9rance dans la tefillah ! \ud83d\udde3\ufe0f Vous avez parfois l'impression que vos pri\u00e8res n'arrivent pas \u00e0 destination ? Les Sages nous enseignent l'importance d'une pri\u00e8re persistante. Il n'y a pas de nombre magique comme \u00ab 20 fois de suite \u00bb, mais l'id\u00e9e centrale est de d\u00e9verser son c\u0153ur avec sinc\u00e9rit\u00e9 et de ne pas abandonner. Pensez \u00e0 un enfant qui demande quelque chose \u00e0 un parent encore et encore parce qu'il en a vraiment besoin ! Avant de formuler vos souhaits, les kabbalistes enseignent une s\u00e9quence puissante : (1) louez D. pour Sa grandeur, (2) remerciez-Le pour toutes les b\u00e9n\u00e9dictions que vous avez d\u00e9j\u00e0. Cela aide \u00e0 ouvrir les \u00ab portes de la pri\u00e8re \u00bb et vous met dans un \u00e9tat de gratitude et de confiance. Continuez \u00e0 prier avec foi et ne d\u00e9sesp\u00e9rez jamais ! Source : D'apr\u00e8s divers enseignements rabbiniques sur la tefillah.

\u041f\u0440\u0435\u0436\u0434\u0435 \u0447\u0435\u043c \u043f\u0440\u043e\u0441\u0438\u0442\u044c \u043e \u0441\u0432\u043e\u0438\u0445 \u0436\u0435\u043b\u0430\u043d\u0438\u044f\u0445, \u043a\u0430\u0431\u0431\u0430\u043b\u0438\u0441\u0442\u044b \u0443\u0447\u0430\u0442 \u043c\u043e\u0449\u043d\u043e\u0439 \u043f\u043e\u0441\u043b\u0435\u0434\u043e\u0432\u0430\u0442\u0435\u043b\u044c\u043d\u043e\u0441\u0442\u0438: (1) \u0432\u043e\u0441\u0445\u0432\u0430\u043b\u0438\u0442\u0435 \u0411-\u0433\u0430 \u0437\u0430 \u0415\u0433\u043e \u0432\u0435\u043b\u0438\u0447\u0438\u0435, (2) \u043f\u043e\u0431\u043b\u0430\u0433\u043e\u0434\u0430\u0440\u0438\u0442\u0435 \u0437\u0430 \u0432\u0441\u0435 \u0431\u043b\u0430\u0433\u043e\u0441\u043b\u043e\u0432\u0435\u043d\u0438\u044f, \u043a\u043e\u0442\u043e\u0440\u044b\u0435 \u0443 \u0432\u0430\u0441 \u0443\u0436\u0435 \u0435\u0441\u0442\u044c. \u042d\u0442\u043e \u043f\u043e\u043c\u043e\u0433\u0430\u0435\u0442 \u043e\u0442\u043a\u0440\u044b\u0442\u044c \u00ab\u0432\u043e\u0440\u043e\u0442\u0430 \u043c\u043e\u043b\u0438\u0442\u0432\u044b\u00bb \u0438 \u043d\u0430\u0441\u0442\u0440\u043e\u0438\u0442\u044c\u0441\u044f \u043d\u0430 \u0431\u043b\u0430\u0433\u043e\u0434\u0430\u0440\u043d\u043e\u0441\u0442\u044c \u0438 \u0434\u043e\u0432\u0435\u0440\u0438\u0435. \u041f\u0440\u043e\u0434\u043e\u043b\u0436\u0430\u0439\u0442\u0435 \u043c\u043e\u043b\u0438\u0442\u044c\u0441\u044f \u0441 \u0432\u0435\u0440\u043e\u0439 \u0438 \u043d\u0438\u043a\u043e\u0433\u0434\u0430 \u043d\u0435 \u043e\u0442\u0447\u0430\u0438\u0432\u0430\u0439\u0442\u0435\u0441\u044c! \u0418\u0441\u0442\u043e\u0447\u043d\u0438\u043a: \u043d\u0430 \u043e\u0441\u043d\u043e\u0432\u0435 \u0440\u0430\u0437\u043b\u0438\u0447\u043d\u044b\u0445 \u0440\u0430\u0432\u0432\u0438\u043d\u0441\u043a\u0438\u0445 \u0443\u0447\u0435\u043d\u0438\u0439 \u043e tefillah.

#3 cloud3 — Learn about the Nazirite vow — a unique spiritual journey

EN Learn about the Nazirite vow \u2014 a unique spiritual journey! \ud83c\udf47\u2702\ufe0f\ud83d\udc80 A Nazir (Nazirite) voluntarily undertakes three powerful abstentions for a minimum of 30 days: (1) No Grape Products: Absolutely nothing from the vine \u2013 no grapes, wine, grape juice, or even grape seeds/skins. This 'fence around the fence' prevents even a hint of indulgence. (2) No Haircuts: The Nazir allows their hair to grow wild, a visible sign of their dedication. At the vow's end, the hair is shaved and brought as an offering. (3) No Contact with the Dead: Even close family members (like a parent or child) cannot be touched, emphasizing a profound level of purity. The ultimate challenge: if the Nazir becomes ritually impure from a corpse, the clock resets! They must shave, bring sacrifices, and start the entire count over. The Torah calls a Nazir 'kadosh' (holy), sparking a fascinating debate among the Sages: Is this extra holiness praiseworthy? The Talmud embraces both perspectives. While no longer widely practiced (because there would be no way to offer the sacrifices required at the end of the nazirite vow period, since there's no Temple) the nazir teaches us about profound self-discipline and the pursuit of holiness. Source: Numbers 6; Rambam, Hilchot Nezirut 1; Talmud, Nazir.
HE \u05d2\u05dc\u05d5 \u05d0\u05ea \u05e0\u05d3\u05e8 \u05d4\u05e0\u05d6\u05d9\u05e8 \u2014 \u05de\u05e1\u05e2 \u05e8\u05d5\u05d7\u05e0\u05d9 \u05d9\u05d9\u05d7\u05d5\u05d3\u05d9! \ud83c\udf47\u2702\ufe0f\ud83d\udc80 \u05e0\u05d6\u05d9\u05e8 \u05e0\u05d5\u05d8\u05dc \u05e2\u05dc \u05e2\u05e6\u05de\u05d5 \u05de\u05e8\u05e6\u05d5\u05df \u05e9\u05dc\u05d5\u05e9 \u05d4\u05d9\u05de\u05e0\u05e2\u05d5\u05d9\u05d5\u05ea \u05e2\u05d5\u05e6\u05de\u05ea\u05d9\u05d5\u05ea \u05dc\u05e4\u05d7\u05d5\u05ea 30 \u05d9\u05d5\u05dd: (1) \u05d1\u05dc\u05d9 \u05de\u05d5\u05e6\u05e8\u05d9 \u05d2\u05e4\u05df: \u05e9\u05d5\u05dd \u05d3\u05d1\u05e8 \u05de\u05d4\u05d2\u05e4\u05df \u2014 \u05dc\u05d0 \u05e2\u05e0\u05d1\u05d9\u05dd, \u05d9\u05d9\u05df, \u05de\u05d9\u05e5 \u05e2\u05e0\u05d1\u05d9\u05dd, \u05d5\u05d0\u05e4\u05d9\u05dc\u05d5 \u05dc\u05d0 \u05d6\u05e8\u05e2\u05d9\u05dd \u05d0\u05d5 \u05e7\u05dc\u05d9\u05e4\u05d5\u05ea. \"\u05d2\u05d3\u05e8 \u05dc\u05d2\u05d3\u05e8\" \u05e9\u05de\u05d5\u05e0\u05e2 \u05db\u05dc \u05e8\u05de\u05d6 \u05dc\u05d4\u05e0\u05d0\u05d4. (2) \u05d1\u05dc\u05d9 \u05ea\u05e1\u05e4\u05d5\u05e8\u05ea: \u05d4\u05e0\u05d6\u05d9\u05e8 \u05de\u05d2\u05d3\u05dc \u05d0\u05ea \u05e9\u05e2\u05e8\u05d5 \u05db\u05e1\u05d9\u05de\u05df \u05e0\u05e8\u05d0\u05d4 \u05dc\u05e2\u05d9\u05df \u05dc\u05d4\u05ea\u05de\u05e1\u05e8\u05d5\u05ea\u05d5. \u05d1\u05e1\u05d9\u05d5\u05dd \u05d4\u05e0\u05d3\u05e8 \u05d4\u05e9\u05e2\u05e8 \u05de\u05d2\u05d5\u05dc\u05d7 \u05d5\u05de\u05d5\u05d1\u05d0 \u05db\u05e7\u05e8\u05d1\u05df. (3) \u05d1\u05dc\u05d9 \u05de\u05d2\u05e2 \u05e2\u05dd \u05de\u05ea\u05d9\u05dd: \u05d0\u05e4\u05d9\u05dc\u05d5 \u05d1\u05e0\u05d9 \u05de\u05e9\u05e4\u05d7\u05d4 \u05e7\u05e8\u05d5\u05d1\u05d9\u05dd \u05d0\u05e1\u05d5\u05e8\u05d9\u05dd \u05d1\u05de\u05d2\u05e2, \u05dc\u05e9\u05dd \u05d3\u05d2\u05e9 \u05e2\u05dc \u05d8\u05d4\u05e8\u05d4 \u05e2\u05de\u05d5\u05e7\u05d4. \u05d4\u05d0\u05ea\u05d2\u05e8 \u05d4\u05d2\u05d3\u05d5\u05dc: \u05d0\u05dd \u05d4\u05e0\u05d6\u05d9\u05e8 \u05e0\u05d8\u05de\u05d0 \u05d1\u05de\u05ea \u2014 \u05d4\u05e9\u05e2\u05d5\u05df \u05de\u05ea\u05d0\u05e4\u05e1! \u05d4\u05d5\u05d0 \u05d7\u05d9\u05d9\u05d1 \u05dc\u05d4\u05ea\u05d2\u05dc\u05d7, \u05dc\u05d4\u05d1\u05d9\u05d0 \u05e7\u05e8\u05d1\u05e0\u05d5\u05ea \u05d5\u05dc\u05d4\u05ea\u05d7\u05d9\u05dc \u05d0\u05ea \u05d4\u05e1\u05e4\u05d9\u05e8\u05d4 \u05de\u05d7\u05d3\u05e9. \u05d4\u05ea\u05d5\u05e8\u05d4 \u05e7\u05d5\u05e8\u05d0\u05ea \u05dc\u05e0\u05d6\u05d9\u05e8 \"\u05e7\u05d3\u05d5\u05e9\", \u05d5\u05d6\u05d4 \u05de\u05e2\u05d5\u05e8\u05e8 \u05d5\u05d9\u05db\u05d5\u05d7 \u05de\u05e8\u05ea\u05e7 \u05d1\u05d9\u05df \u05d4\u05d7\u05db\u05de\u05d9\u05dd: \u05d4\u05d0\u05dd \u05d4\u05d4\u05ea\u05e7\u05d3\u05e9\u05d5\u05ea \u05d4\u05e0\u05d5\u05e1\u05e4\u05ea \u05d4\u05d6\u05d5 \u05e8\u05d0\u05d5\u05d9\u05d4 \u05dc\u05e9\u05d1\u05d7? \u05d4\u05ea\u05dc\u05de\u05d5\u05d3 \u05de\u05db\u05d9\u05dc \u05d0\u05ea \u05e9\u05ea\u05d9 \u05d4\u05d3\u05e2\u05d5\u05ea. \u05dc\u05de\u05e8\u05d5\u05ea \u05e9\u05db\u05d9\u05d5\u05dd \u05db\u05de\u05e2\u05d8 \u05dc\u05d0 \u05e0\u05d5\u05d4\u05d2\u05d9\u05dd \u05d1\u05db\u05da (\u05db\u05d9 \u05d0\u05d9\u05df \u05d1\u05d9\u05ea \u05de\u05e7\u05d3\u05e9 \u05dc\u05d4\u05e7\u05e8\u05d1\u05ea \u05d4\u05e7\u05e8\u05d1\u05e0\u05d5\u05ea \u05d1\u05e1\u05d9\u05d5\u05dd), \u05d4\u05e0\u05d6\u05d9\u05e8 \u05de\u05dc\u05de\u05d3 \u05d0\u05d5\u05ea\u05e0\u05d5 \u05e2\u05dc \u05de\u05e9\u05de\u05e2\u05ea \u05e2\u05e6\u05de\u05d9\u05ea \u05e2\u05de\u05d5\u05e7\u05d4 \u05d5\u05e8\u05d3\u05d9\u05e4\u05ea \u05e7\u05d3\u05d5\u05e9\u05d4. \u05de\u05e7\u05d5\u05e8: \u05d1\u05de\u05d3\u05d1\u05e8 \u05d5; \u05e8\u05de\u05d1\"\u05dd, \u05d4\u05dc\u05db\u05d5\u05ea \u05e0\u05d6\u05d9\u05e8\u05d5\u05ea \u05d0; \u05ea\u05dc\u05de\u05d5\u05d3, \u05e0\u05d6\u05d9\u05e8.
ES \u00a1Conoce el voto nazir \u2014 un viaje espiritual \u00fanico! \ud83c\udf47\u2702\ufe0f\ud83d\udc80 Un nazir (nazareo) asume voluntariamente tres abstenciones poderosas por un m\u00ednimo de 30 d\u00edas: (1) Sin productos de uva: nada de la vid \u2014 ni uvas, vino, jugo de uva, ni siquiera semillas o pieles. Un \"cerco alrededor del cerco\" que evita cualquier indicio de indulgencia. (2) Sin cortes de pelo: el nazir deja crecer su cabello como se\u00f1al visible de dedicaci\u00f3n. Al final del voto, el cabello se rapea y se ofrece como sacrificio. (3) Sin contacto con los muertos: ni siquiera familiares cercanos pueden ser tocados, enfatizando un nivel profundo de pureza. El desaf\u00edo m\u00e1ximo: si el nazir se contamina por un cad\u00e1ver, \u00a1el reloj se reinicia! Debe raparse, traer sacrificios y empezar de nuevo. La Tor\u00e1 llama al nazir \"kadosh\" (santo), lo que genera un debate fascinante entre los Sabios: \u00bfes esta santidad extra loable? El Talmud abraza ambas perspectivas. Aunque ya no se practica ampliamente (porque no hay Templo para los sacrificios al final), el nazir nos ense\u00f1a disciplina profunda y la b\u00fasqueda de santidad. Fuente: N\u00fameros 6; Rambam, Hilchot Nezirut 1; Talmud, Nazir.
FR D\u00e9couvrez le v\u0153u de nazir \u2014 un voyage spirituel unique ! \ud83c\udf47\u2702\ufe0f\ud83d\udc80 Un nazir (nazir\u00e9en) s'engage volontairement \u00e0 trois abstentions puissantes pendant au moins 30 jours : (1) Aucun produit de la vigne : rien de la vigne \u2014 ni raisins, ni vin, ni jus de raisin, ni m\u00eame p\u00e9pins ou peaux. Une \u00ab cl\u00f4ture autour de la cl\u00f4ture \u00bb qui emp\u00eache toute indulgence. (2) Pas de coupe de cheveux : le nazir laisse pousser ses cheveux comme signe visible de d\u00e9votion. \u00c0 la fin du v\u0153u, les cheveux sont ras\u00e9s et offerts en sacrifice. (3) Aucun contact avec les morts : m\u00eame les proches parents ne peuvent \u00eatre touch\u00e9s, soulignant un niveau profond de puret\u00e9. Le d\u00e9fi ultime : si le nazir devient impur par un cadavre, le compteur repart \u00e0 z\u00e9ro ! Il doit se raser, apporter des sacrifices et recommencer. La Torah appelle le nazir \u00ab kadosh \u00bb (saint), ce qui suscite un d\u00e9bat fascinant parmi les Sages : cette saintet\u00e9 suppl\u00e9mentaire est-elle louable ? Le Talmud embrasse les deux perspectives. Bien que peu pratiqu\u00e9 aujourd'hui (car il n'y a plus de Temple pour les sacrifices de fin de v\u0153u), le nazir nous enseigne une profonde discipline et la qu\u00eate de saintet\u00e9. Source : Nombres 6 ; Rambam, Hilchot Nezirut 1 ; Talmud, Nazir.

(2) \u0411\u0435\u0437 \u0441\u0442\u0440\u0438\u0436\u043a\u0438: \u043d\u0430\u0437\u0438\u0440 \u043e\u0442\u043f\u0443\u0441\u043a\u0430\u0435\u0442 \u0432\u043e\u043b\u043e\u0441\u044b \u043a\u0430\u043a \u0432\u0438\u0434\u0438\u043c\u044b\u0439 \u0437\u043d\u0430\u043a \u043f\u043e\u0441\u0432\u044f\u0449\u0435\u043d\u0438\u044f. \u0412 \u043a\u043e\u043d\u0446\u0435 \u043e\u0431\u0435\u0442\u0430 \u0432\u043e\u043b\u043e\u0441\u044b \u0441\u0431\u0440\u0438\u0432\u0430\u044e\u0442\u0441\u044f \u0438 \u043f\u0440\u0438\u043d\u043e\u0441\u044f\u0442\u0441\u044f \u0432 \u0436\u0435\u0440\u0442\u0432\u0443. #4 cloud4 — Ever dreamed of being a king? 👑 Discover the surprising halachot (laws) of a Jew

EN Ever dreamed of being a king? \ud83d\udc51 Discover the surprising halachot (laws) of a Jewish King! Unlike other monarchs, a Jewish King had strict limits to keep him humble and focused on Hashem. For example, he couldn't acquire too many wives (to avoid his heart turning away from God - a maximum of 18, according to the Talmud), or too many horses (so he'd rely on Divine protection, not military might), or excessive silver and gold (to prevent arrogance). His primary role wasn't just ruling, but being a spiritual shepherd, a scholar immersed in Torah, and a righteous judge. These laws teach us that true leadership in Judaism is about humility, integrity, and putting the welfare of the people (and God's will) first. Even if you're not royalty, you can try to embody these kingly qualities in your own life!

ES \u00bfAlguna vez so\u00f1aste con ser rey? \ud83d\udc51 \u00a1Descubre las sorprendentes halajot (leyes) de un rey jud\u00edo! A diferencia de otros monarcas, un rey jud\u00edo ten\u00eda l\u00edmites estrictos para mantenerlo humilde y enfocado en Hashem. Por ejemplo, no pod\u00eda adquirir demasiadas esposas (para que su coraz\u00f3n no se desviara \u2014 m\u00e1ximo 18, seg\u00fan el Talmud), ni demasiados caballos (para confiar en la protecci\u00f3n divina, no en la fuerza militar), ni plata y oro en exceso (para evitar la arrogancia). Su rol principal no era solo gobernar, sino ser pastor espiritual, erudito inmerso en la Tor\u00e1 y juez justo. Estas leyes nos ense\u00f1an que el verdadero liderazgo en el juda\u00edsmo es humildad, integridad y poner el bienestar del pueblo (y la voluntad de D-s) primero. Aunque no seas realeza, \u00a1puedes encarnar estas cualidades reales en tu vida!
FR Vous avez r\u00eav\u00e9 d'\u00eatre roi ? \ud83d\udc51 D\u00e9couvrez les halachot (lois) surprenantes d'un roi juif ! Contrairement aux autres monarques, un roi juif avait des limites strictes pour rester humble et concentr\u00e9 sur D. Par exemple, il ne pouvait pas prendre trop d'\u00e9pouses (pour que son c\u0153ur ne d\u00e9vie pas \u2014 maximum 18, selon le Talmud), ni trop de chevaux (pour s'appuyer sur la protection divine, pas sur la force militaire), ni d'argent et d'or en exc\u00e8s (pour \u00e9viter l'arrogance). Son r\u00f4le principal n'\u00e9tait pas seulement de r\u00e9gner, mais d'\u00eatre un berger spirituel, un \u00e9rudit plong\u00e9 dans la Torah et un juge juste. Ces lois nous enseignent que le vrai leadership dans le juda\u00efsme, c'est l'humilit\u00e9, l'int\u00e9grit\u00e9 et le bien-\u00eatre du peuple (et la volont\u00e9 de D.) avant tout. M\u00eame si vous n'\u00eates pas de la royaut\u00e9, vous pouvez incarner ces qualit\u00e9s royales dans votre vie !

#5 cloud5 — Get ready to experience the Sukkah spirit

EN Get ready to experience the Sukkah spirit! \u26fa\ufe0f During Sukkot, we have the special mitzvah of dwelling in a Sukkah \u2013 a temporary booth \u2013 just like camping, but with a huge spiritual punch! This unique dwelling reminds us of the clouds of glory that protected us in the desert and the fragility of life, encouraging us to trust completely in Hashem. What does 'dwelling' mean? It primarily means eating your meals there. For sleeping, the Shulchan Aruch (Orach Chaim 639) rules that men are obligated to sleep in the Sukkah, but women are exempt (though many choose to sleep there if comfortable). Sephardi practice is generally to be more stringent about sleeping in the Sukkah even if uncomfortable, while Ashkenazim are more lenient if there's significant discomfort (e.g., cold, rain, or a bad smell). The Talmud teaches that the Shechinah (Divine Presence) literally rests in a kosher Sukkah \u2013 no wonder it's a favorite holiday for so many! So, even if you can't build a full Sukkah, reflect on its themes of impermanence and Divine protection.

ES \u00a1Prep\u00e1rate para vivir el esp\u00edritu de la Suc\u00e1! \u26fa\ufe0f Durante Sucot tenemos la mitzv\u00e1 especial de habitar en una suc\u00e1 \u2014 una caba\u00f1a temporal \u2014 como acampar, \u00a1pero con un gran impacto espiritual! Esta morada nos recuerda las nubes de gloria que nos protegieron en el desierto y la fragilidad de la vida, anim\u00e1ndonos a confiar plenamente en Hashem. \u00bfQu\u00e9 significa \"habitar\"? Principalmente comer las comidas all\u00ed. Para dormir, el Shulj\u00e1n Aruj (Oraj Jaim 639) establece que los hombres est\u00e1n obligados a dormir en la suc\u00e1, y las mujeres est\u00e1n exentas (aunque muchas eligen hacerlo si es c\u00f3modo). La pr\u00e1ctica sefard\u00ed suele ser m\u00e1s estricta incluso con incomodidad, mientras los asquenaz\u00edes son m\u00e1s flexibles ante molestias significativas (fr\u00edo, lluvia o mal olor). El Talmud ense\u00f1a que la Shejin\u00e1 (Presencia Divina) reposa literalmente en una suc\u00e1 kosher \u2014 \u00a1no es de extra\u00f1ar que sea una fiesta tan querida! Si no puedes construir una suc\u00e1 completa, reflexiona sobre la impermanencia y la protecci\u00f3n divina.
FR Pr\u00e9parez-vous \u00e0 vivre l'esprit de la Soucca ! \u26fa\ufe0f Pendant Souccot, nous avons la mitzvah sp\u00e9ciale d'habiter dans une soucca \u2014 une cabane temporaire \u2014 comme du camping, mais avec un immense impact spirituel ! Que signifie \u00ab habiter \u00bb ? Principalement y prendre ses repas. Pour le sommeil, le Choulhan Aroukh (Ora'h 'Ha\u00efm 639) statue que les hommes sont tenus de dormir dans la soucca, et les femmes en sont exempt\u00e9es (bien que beaucoup choisissent d'y dormir si c'est confortable). La pratique s\u00e9farade est g\u00e9n\u00e9ralement plus stricte m\u00eame en cas d'inconfort, tandis que les ashk\u00e9nazes sont plus souples face \u00e0 une g\u00eane significative (froid, pluie ou mauvaise odeur). Le Talmud enseigne que la Chekhinah (Pr\u00e9sence divine) repose litt\u00e9ralement dans une soucca casher \u2014 pas \u00e9tonnant que ce soit une f\u00eate si ch\u00e8re ! M\u00eame si vous ne pouvez pas construire une soucca compl\u00e8te, m\u00e9ditez sur l'impermanence et la protection divine.

#6 cloud6 — Get ready for a wake-up call

EN Get ready for a wake-up call! \ud83c\udfba Explore the awesome mitzvah of blowing the Shofar on Rosh Hashanah! This isn't just about making noise; it's a powerful spiritual alarm clock for our souls, urging us toward introspection and Teshuva (repentance). The Shofar's blasts have deep meaning: Tekiah is a long, unbroken blast, symbolizing clarity, certainty, and our unified connection to Hashem. Shevarim consists of three shorter, broken blasts, evoking a sigh or cry, representing our brokenness and heartfelt regret for our shortcomings. Teruah is a series of at least nine rapid, staccato blasts, like rapid sobbing, signifying a desperate plea for Divine mercy and a readiness for spiritual awakening. The sequence of these sounds (Tekiah-Shevarim-Teruah-Tekiah, etc.) is crucial. Imagine these ancient sounds piercing the air on the Day of Judgment, stirring your soul to return to your Creator. Source: Numbers 29:1; Talmud, Rosh Hashanah 33b; Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim 590.

ES \u00a1Prep\u00e1rate para un despertar! \ud83c\udfba Explora la incre\u00edble mitzv\u00e1 de tocar el shofar en Rosh Hashan\u00e1. No es solo hacer ruido: es una poderosa alarma espiritual para el alma, que nos impulsa a la introspecci\u00f3n y al teshuv\u00e1 (arrepentimiento). Cada sonido tiene un significado profundo: Teki\u00e1 es un blast largo e ininterrumpido, que simboliza claridad, certeza y nuestra conexi\u00f3n unificada con Hashem. Shevarim son tres blasts cortos y quebrados, como un suspiro o llanto, que expresan nuestra fragilidad y arrepentimiento sincero. Teru\u00e1 es una serie de al menos nueve blasts r\u00e1pidos, como sollozos, que significan una s\u00faplica desesperada por misericordia divina. La secuencia (Teki\u00e1-Shevarim-Teru\u00e1-Teki\u00e1, etc.) es crucial. Imagina estos sonidos antiguos en el D\u00eda del Juicio, despertando tu alma para volver a tu Creador. Fuente: N\u00fameros 29:1; Talmud, Rosh Hashan\u00e1 33b; Shulj\u00e1n Aruj, Oraj Jaim 590.

#7 cloud7 — Want to be a superstar kid (or adult)? 👨‍👩‍👧‍👦 Discover the incredibly important

EN Want to be a superstar kid (or adult)? \ud83d\udc68\u200d\ud83d\udc69\u200d\ud83d\udc67\u200d\ud83d\udc66 Discover the incredibly important mitzvah of Kibud Av Va'em (Honoring your Father and Mother)! It's one of the Ten Commandments, and it's more than just saying 'thank you.' It's about deep respect, ensuring their comfort, caring for them as they age, and bringing them nachas (joy/pride) through your actions. This mitzvah teaches gratitude, humility, and recognizing the chain of tradition. What's super cool? The Gemara (Kiddushin 31a) teaches that there's NO limit to honoring parents \u2013 every moment is an opportunity! Even if they've passed on, we honor them by learning Torah, performing mitzvot, and dedicating acts of kindness in their memory. So, think of one specific act you can do today to make your parents proud, whether they're with you or in the Olam Haba (World to Come)!

ES \u00bfQuieres ser un ni\u00f1o (o adulto) estrella? \ud83d\udc68\u200d\ud83d\udc69\u200d\ud83d\udc67\u200d\ud83d\udc66 \u00a1Descubre la mitzv\u00e1 incre\u00edblemente importante de Kibud Av Va'em (honrar a padre y madre)! Es uno de los Diez Mandamientos, y va mucho m\u00e1s all\u00e1 de decir \"gracias\". Es respeto profundo, cuidar su comodidad, atenderlos en la vejez y darles nach\u00e1s (orgullo/alegr\u00eda) con tus acciones. Esta mitzv\u00e1 ense\u00f1a gratitud, humildad y reconocer la cadena de tradici\u00f3n. \u00bfLo m\u00e1s genial? El Guemar\u00e1 (Kidushin 31a) ense\u00f1a que no hay l\u00edmite para honrar a los padres \u2014 \u00a1cada momento es una oportunidad! Incluso si ya fallecieron, los honramos estudiando Tor\u00e1, cumpliendo mitzvot y haciendo actos de bondad en su memoria. Piensa en un acto espec\u00edfico que puedas hacer hoy para enorgullecer a tus padres, est\u00e9n contigo o en el Olam Haba (Mundo Venidero).
FR Envie d'\u00eatre un enfant (ou un adulte) superstar ? \ud83d\udc68\u200d\ud83d\udc69\u200d\ud83d\udc67\u200d\ud83d\udc66 D\u00e9couvrez la mitzvah incroyablement importante de Kiboud Av Va'em (honorer p\u00e8re et m\u00e8re) ! C'est l'un des Dix Commandements, et c'est bien plus que dire \u00ab merci \u00bb. C'est un profond respect, veiller \u00e0 leur confort, prendre soin d'eux dans la vieillesse et leur donner du nachat (fiert\u00e9/joie) par vos actions. Cette mitzvah enseigne la gratitude, l'humilit\u00e9 et la reconnaissance de la cha\u00eene de tradition. Le plus cool ? Le Gu\u00e9mara (Kiddouchin 31a) enseigne qu'il n'y a AUCUNE limite \u00e0 l'honneur d\u00fb aux parents \u2014 chaque instant est une opportunit\u00e9 ! M\u00eame s'ils sont d\u00e9c\u00e9d\u00e9s, nous les honorons en \u00e9tudiant la Torah, en accomplissant des mitzvot et en faisant des actes de bont\u00e9 en leur m\u00e9moire. Pensez \u00e0 un acte pr\u00e9cis que vous pouvez faire aujourd'hui pour rendre vos parents fiers, qu'ils soient avec vous ou dans l'Olam Haba (Monde \u00e0 Venir) !

#8 cloud8 — Learn the #1 Constant Mitzvah

EN Learn the #1 Constant Mitzvah! Did you know there are six special mitzvot you can fulfill every single moment, no matter where you are or what you're doing? The very first is to know that Hashem (God) exists! This isn't just believing; it's about recognizing and internalizing that God is the Creator of everything and is actively involved in sustaining and guiding the entire world, right now! Take a moment, look around you, and marvel at the intricate design and vastness of the universe, and reflect on the miracle of your own existence. This constant awareness deepens your relationship with the Creator.
HE \u05dc\u05de\u05d3\u05d5 \u05d0\u05ea \u05de\u05e6\u05d5\u05d5\u05d4 \u05e7\u05d1\u05d5\u05e2\u05d4 \u05de\u05e1\u05e4\u05e8 1! \u05d9\u05d3\u05e2\u05ea\u05dd \u05e9\u05d9\u05e9 \u05e9\u05e9 \u05de\u05e6\u05d5\u05d5\u05ea \u05de\u05d9\u05d5\u05d7\u05d3\u05d5\u05ea \u05e9\u05d0\u05e4\u05e9\u05e8 \u05dc\u05e7\u05d9\u05d9\u05dd \u05d1\u05db\u05dc \u05e8\u05d2\u05e2, \u05d1\u05db\u05dc \u05de\u05e7\u05d5\u05dd \u05d5\u05d1\u05db\u05dc \u05e4\u05e2\u05d9\u05dc\u05d5\u05ea? \u05d4\u05e8\u05d0\u05e9\u05d5\u05e0\u05d4 \u05d4\u05d9\u05d0 \u05dc\u05d3\u05e2\u05ea \u05e9\u05d4' \u05e7\u05d9\u05d9\u05dd! \u05d6\u05d4 \u05dc\u05d0 \u05e8\u05e7 \u05dc\u05d4\u05d0\u05de\u05d9\u05df \u2014 \u05d6\u05d4 \u05dc\u05d4\u05db\u05d9\u05e8 \u05d5\u05dc\u05d4\u05d8\u05de\u05d9\u05e2 \u05e9\u05d1\u05d5\u05e8\u05d0 \u05d4\u05e2\u05d5\u05dc\u05dd \u05d4\u05d5\u05d0 \u05d1\u05d5\u05e8\u05d0 \u05d4\u05db\u05dc \u05d5\u05de\u05e2\u05d5\u05e8\u05d1 \u05d1\u05d0\u05d5\u05e4\u05df \u05e4\u05e2\u05d9\u05dc \u05d1\u05d4\u05d7\u05d6\u05e7\u05ea \u05d4\u05e2\u05d5\u05dc\u05dd \u05d5\u05d4\u05e0\u05d7\u05d9\u05d9\u05ea\u05d5, \u05de\u05de\u05e9 \u05e2\u05db\u05e9\u05d9\u05d5! \u05e2\u05e6\u05e8\u05d5 \u05e8\u05d2\u05e2, \u05d4\u05e1\u05ea\u05db\u05dc\u05d5 \u05e1\u05d1\u05d9\u05d1\u05db\u05dd, \u05d4\u05ea\u05e4\u05e2\u05dc\u05d5 \u05de\u05d4\u05e2\u05d9\u05e6\u05d5\u05d1 \u05d4\u05de\u05d5\u05e8\u05db\u05d1 \u05d5\u05de\u05d4\u05d9\u05e7\u05e3 \u05d4\u05d9\u05e7\u05d5\u05dd, \u05d5\u05d4\u05ea\u05d1\u05d5\u05e0\u05e0\u05d5 \u05d1\u05e0\u05d9\u05e1 \u05e9\u05dc \u05e7\u05d9\u05d5\u05de\u05db\u05dd. \u05d4\u05de\u05d5\u05d3\u05e2\u05d5\u05ea \u05d4\u05e7\u05d1\u05d5\u05e2\u05d4 \u05d4\u05d6\u05d5 \u05de\u05e2\u05de\u05d9\u05e7\u05d4 \u05d0\u05ea \u05d4\u05e7\u05e9\u05e8 \u05e2\u05dd \u05d4\u05d1\u05d5\u05e8\u05d0.
ES \u00a1Aprende la mitzv\u00e1 constante #1! \u00bfSab\u00edas que hay seis mitzvot especiales que puedes cumplir en cada momento, sin importar d\u00f3nde est\u00e9s o qu\u00e9 hagas? #9 cloud9 — Discover #2 of the Constant Mitzvot: Don't believe in any other powers

EN Discover #2 of the Constant Mitzvot: Don't believe in any other powers! \ud83d\udeab This isn't just about avoiding idol worship; it's about deeply internalizing that Hashem is the *only* true power in the universe. Everything \u2013 from the smallest atom to the grandest galaxy \u2013 is completely under His control. Nothing can act without His permission! Take a moment to recognize that every event, every challenge, and every blessing you experience is directly from Him, with no intermediary forces or independent powers. This profound belief brings immense trust and peace of mind. Source: Exodus 20:3; Rambam, Sefer HaMitzvot, Negative Commandment 2; Mishneh Torah, Avodat Kochavim 2:1.

#10 cloud10 — Explore #3 of the Constant Mitzvot: Know that Hashem is One

EN Explore #3 of the Constant Mitzvot: Know that Hashem is One! \u261d\ufe0f This isn't just about a numerical unity; it's about understanding that God is absolutely unique, indivisible, and utterly beyond our comprehension \u2013 the ultimate singularity! He is the source of all existence, which is completely unified in His essence and power. When you say the first line of Shema Yisrael, focus deeply on this profound truth. Many have the custom to close their eyes during this line to block out distractions and concentrate entirely on Hashem's absolute unity. You can fulfill this mitzvah any time by contemplating God's oneness and His singular control over the universe. Source: Deuteronomy 6:4; Rambam, Sefer HaMitzvot, Positive Commandment 2; Mishneh Torah, Yesodei HaTorah 1:7.

#11 cloud11 — Experience #4 of the Constant Mitzvot: Love Hashem

EN Experience #4 of the Constant Mitzvot: Love Hashem! \u2764\ufe0f This isn't just a feeling; it's an active mitzvah to constantly cultivate a deep love for God. How do you do that? By reflecting on all the incredible kindnesses Hashem bestows upon you every single moment \u2013 from keeping your heart beating to orchestrating every detail of your life for your ultimate good. The more you recognize His constant presence and boundless benevolence, the more your love and appreciation for Him will naturally grow. Take a moment now to list five specific amazing/miraculous things Hashem has done for you \u2013 and thank Him with love! Source: Deuteronomy 6:5; Rambam, Sefer HaMitzvot, Positive Commandment 3; Mishneh Torah, Yesodei HaTorah 2:2.

#12 cloud12 — Contemplate #5 of the Constant Mitzvot: Be in awe of Hashem

EN Contemplate #5 of the Constant Mitzvot: Be in awe of Hashem! \ud83e\udd29 This isn't just about fear; it's about recognizing God's immense power, majesty, and transcendence, inspiring profound reverence. Imagine the splitting of the Red Sea or standing at Mount Sinai \u2013 that sense of overwhelming grandeur is what Yirat Hashem (Awe of G-d) is all about! This awareness helps us appreciate the significance of every mitzvah and realize that every action we take matters. It guides us to make choices that are aligned with spiritual truth and connect us to what's truly important in life. Source: Deuteronomy 6:13; Rambam, Sefer HaMitzvot, Positive Commandment 4; Mishneh Torah, Yesodei HaTorah 2:2.

#13 cloud13 — Master #6 of the Constant Mitzvot: Don't be led astray by your eyes and heart

EN Master #6 of the Constant Mitzvot: Don't be led astray by your eyes and heart! \ud83d\udc40\u2764\ufe0f This mitzvah (Numbers 15:39) reminds us to guard our thoughts and desires from pulling us away from Torah values and Hashem. It's an ongoing spiritual battle! When you notice yourself being drawn towards something that doesn't align with kedusha (holiness) or when your mind wanders into non-Torah philosophies, you have an immediate opportunity to fulfill this mitzvah. Staying focused on Torah, its wisdom, and its immense rewards is the ultimate key to true happiness and connection. This mitzvah requires constant vigilance and self-control. Source: Numbers 15:39; Rambam, Sefer HaMitzvot, Negative Commandment 3; Mishneh Torah, Avodat Kochavim 2:3.

#14 cloud14 — Guard your body, mind, and soul — they're gifts from Hashem

EN Guard your body, mind, and soul \u2014 they're gifts from Hashem! \ud83d\udcab This mitzvah isn't just about physical health; it's a holistic approach to serving G-d. The Rambam (Hilchot De'ot 3:3) teaches that maintaining your health is a Torah obligation, because 'it is impossible to understand and know G-d when one is sick or hungry.' Your body is the vessel for your soul's mission \u2014 a fit body supports a healthy spiritual life. For your MIND: engage in Torah study, which sharpens your intellect and purifies your thoughts. Avoid excessive worry and grudges, as they can harm both mind and body. For your SOUL: nurture it with regular prayer, mitzvot, and acts of kindness, strengthening its connection to its Divine Source. Simcha (joy) is also a crucial spiritual obligation; sadness can be a major barrier to spiritual growth. Practical takeaway: eat well, get enough sleep, exercise, and constantly seek joy. These aren't luxuries; they're spiritual necessities! Source: Deuteronomy 4:15; Rambam, Hilchot De'ot 3:3; Sefer HaChinuch, Mitzvah 225.

#15 cloud15 — Say the Shema — the ultimate declaration of Jewish faith

EN Say the Shema \u2014 the ultimate declaration of Jewish faith! \ud83d\udde3\ufe0f 'Hear O Israel, the Lord our G-d, the Lord is One.' This iconic verse is arguably the most important sentence a Jew says in their entire life! It's often the first sentence a Jewish child learns, and often the last words spoken before passing on. We say it twice daily (morning and night) as a Torah commandment. The halacha requires saying Shema with enough kavanah (concentration) to understand its meaning, at least for the first verse, and clearly enough to hear yourself. A powerful story: Rabbi Akiva, while being tortured to death by the Romans, declared that he had yearned his whole life to fulfill 'love G-d with all your soul' even if it meant giving his life \u2013 and he died with 'Echad' (One) on his lips.
HE \u05d0\u05de\u05e8\u05d5 \u05d0\u05ea \u05e9\u05de\u05e2 \u2014 \u05d4\u05d4\u05db\u05e8\u05d6\u05d4 \u05d4\u05d2\u05d3\u05d5\u05dc\u05d4 \u05d1\u05d9\u05d5\u05ea\u05e8 \u05e2\u05dc \u05d0\u05de\u05d5\u05e0\u05ea \u05d9\u05e9\u05e8\u05d0\u05dc! \ud83d\udde3\ufe0f \"\u05e9\u05de\u05e2 \u05d9\u05e9\u05e8\u05d0\u05dc \u05d4' \u05d0\u05dc\u05d5\u05e7\u05d9\u05e0\u05d5 \u05d4' \u05d0\u05d7\u05d3.\" \u05d4\u05e4\u05e1\u05d5\u05e7 \u05d4\u05d0\u05d9\u05e7\u05d5\u05e0\u05d9 \u05d4\u05d6\u05d4 \u05d4\u05d5\u05d0 \u05db\u05e0\u05e8\u05d0\u05d4 \u05d4\u05de\u05e9\u05e4\u05d8 \u05d4\u05d7\u05e9\u05d5\u05d1 \u05d1\u05d9\u05d5\u05ea\u05e8 \u05e9\u05d9\u05d4\u05d5\u05d3\u05d9 \u05d0\u05d5\u05de\u05e8 \u05d1\u05d7\u05d9\u05d9\u05d5! \u05dc\u05e8\u05d5\u05d1 \u05d6\u05d4 \u05d4\u05de\u05e9\u05e4\u05d8 \u05d4\u05e8\u05d0\u05e9\u05d5\u05df \u05e9\u05d9\u05dc\u05d3 \u05d9\u05d4\u05d5\u05d3\u05d9 \u05dc\u05d5\u05de\u05d3, \u05d5\u05dc\u05e2\u05d9\u05ea\u05d9\u05dd \u05d4\u05d0\u05d7\u05e8\u05d5\u05e0\u05d5\u05ea \u05dc\u05e4\u05e0\u05d9 \u05d4\u05e1\u05ea\u05dc\u05e7\u05d5\u05ea. \u05d0\u05d5\u05de\u05e8\u05d9\u05dd \u05d0\u05d5\u05ea\u05d5 \u05e4\u05e2\u05de\u05d9\u05d9\u05dd \u05d1\u05d9\u05d5\u05dd (\u05d1\u05d5\u05e7\u05e8 \u05d5\u05e2\u05e8\u05d1) \u05db\u05de\u05e6\u05d5\u05d5\u05ea \u05ea\u05d5\u05e8\u05d4. \u05d4\u05d4\u05dc\u05db\u05d4 \u05d3\u05d5\u05e8\u05e9\u05ea \u05dc\u05d5\u05de\u05e8 \u05e9\u05de\u05e2 \u05d1\u05db\u05d5\u05d5\u05e0\u05d4 \u05de\u05e1\u05e4\u05e7\u05ea \u05dc\u05d4\u05d1\u05d9\u05df \u05d0\u05ea \u05d4\u05de\u05e9\u05de\u05e2\u05d5\u05ea, \u05dc\u05e4\u05d7\u05d5\u05ea \u05d1\u05e4\u05e1\u05d5\u05e7 \u05d4\u05e8\u05d0\u05e9\u05d5\u05df, \u05d5\u05d1\u05d1\u05d9\u05e8\u05d5\u05e8 \u05e9\u05e9\u05d5\u05de\u05e2\u05d9\u05dd \u05d0\u05ea \u05e2\u05e6\u05de\u05db\u05dd. \u05e1\u05d9\u05e4\u05d5\u05e8 \u05e2\u05d5\u05e6\u05de\u05ea\u05d9: \u05e8\u05d1\u05d9 \u05e2\u05e7\u05d9\u05d1\u05d0, \u05d1\u05d6\u05de\u05df \u05e2\u05d9\u05e0\u05d5\u05d9\u05d9\u05dd \u05e2\u05dc \u05d9\u05d3\u05d9 \u05d4\u05e8\u05d5\u05de\u05d0\u05d9\u05dd, \u05d0\u05de\u05e8 \u05e9\u05db\u05dc \u05d7\u05d9\u05d9\u05d5 \u05d7\u05d9\u05db\u05d4 \u05dc\u05e7\u05d9\u05d9\u05dd \"\u05d5\u05d0\u05d4\u05d1\u05ea \u05d0\u05ea \u05d4' \u05d0\u05dc\u05d5\u05e7\u05d9\u05da \u05d1\u05db\u05dc \u05e0\u05e4\u05e9\u05da\" \u05d2\u05dd \u05d0\u05dd \u05d6\u05d4 \u05d0\u05d5\u05de\u05e8 \u05dc\u05de\u05e1\u05d5\u05e8 \u05d0\u05ea \u05e0\u05e4\u05e9\u05d5 \u2014 \u05d5\u05e0\u05e4\u05d8\u05e8 \u05e2\u05dd \"\u05d0\u05d7\u05d3\" \u05e2\u05dc \u05e9\u05e4\u05ea\u05d9\u05d5.
ES \u00a1Di el Shem\u00e1 \u2014 la declaraci\u00f3n suprema de fe jud\u00eda! \ud83d\udde3\ufe0f \"Escucha, Israel: Hashem es nuestro D-s, Hashem es Uno.\" Este vers\u00edculo ic\u00f3nico es posiblemente la frase m\u00e1s importante que un jud\u00edo dice en toda su vida. Suele ser la primera que aprende un ni\u00f1o jud\u00edo, y a menudo las \u00faltimas palabras antes de partir. Lo decimos dos veces al d\u00eda (ma\u00f1ana y noche) como mandamiento de la Tor\u00e1. La halaj\u00e1 exige decir el Shem\u00e1 con suficiente kavan\u00e1 (concentraci\u00f3n) para entender su significado, al menos el primer vers\u00edculo, y con claridad para o\u00edrse a uno mismo. Una historia poderosa: el rabino Akiva, torturado por los romanos, declar\u00f3 que hab\u00eda anhelado cumplir \"ama a D-s con toda tu alma\" incluso si significaba dar la vida \u2014 y muri\u00f3 con \"Ejad\" (Uno) en los labios.
FR R\u00e9citez le Shema \u2014 la d\u00e9claration supr\u00eame de la foi juive ! \ud83d\udde3\ufe0f \u00ab \u00c9coute, Isra\u00ebl : l'\u00c9ternel est notre D., l'\u00c9ternel est Un. \u00bb Ce verset iconique est sans doute la phrase la plus importante qu'un Juif prononce dans sa vie ! C'est souvent la premi\u00e8re qu'un enfant juif apprend, et souvent les derni\u00e8res avant de partir. Nous le r\u00e9citons deux fois par jour (matin et soir) comme commandement de la Torah. La halacha exige de dire le Shema avec assez de kavanah (concentration) pour en comprendre le sens, au moins pour le premier verset, et assez clairement pour s'entendre. Une histoire puissante : Rabbi Akiva, tortur\u00e9 \u00e0 mort par les Romains, d\u00e9clara qu'il avait attendu toute sa vie d'accomplir \u00ab aime D. de toute ton \u00e2me \u00bb m\u00eame si cela signifiait donner sa vie \u2014 et il mourut avec \u00ab E'had \u00bb (Un) sur les l\u00e8vres.
RU \u041f\u0440\u043e\u0438\u0437\u043d\u0435\u0441\u0438\u0442\u0435 \u0428\u043c\u0430 \u2014 \u0433\u043b\u0430\u0432\u043d\u043e\u0435 \u043f\u0440\u043e\u0432\u043e\u0437\u0433\u043b\u0430\u0448\u0435\u043d\u0438\u0435 \u0435\u0432\u0440\u0435\u0439\u0441\u043a\u043e\u0439 \u0432\u0435\u0440\u044b! \ud83d\udde3\ufe0f \u00ab\u0421\u043b\u0443\u0448\u0430\u0439, \u0418\u0437\u0440\u0430\u0438\u043b\u044c: \u0413-\u0441\u043f\u043e\u0434\u044c \u0411-\u0433 \u043d\u0430\u0448, \u0413-\u0441\u043f\u043e\u0434\u044c \u0435\u0434\u0438\u043d\u00bb. \u042d\u0442\u043e\u0442 \u0437\u043d\u0430\u043a\u043e\u0432\u044b\u0439 \u0441\u0442\u0438\u0445 \u2014 \u0432\u043e\u0437\u043c\u043e\u0436\u043d\u043e, \u0441\u0430\u043c\u043e\u0435 \u0432\u0430\u0436\u043d\u043e\u0435 \u043f\u0440\u0435\u0434\u043b\u043e\u0436\u0435\u043d\u0438\u0435, \u043a\u043e\u0442\u043e\u0440\u043e\u0435 \u0435\u0432\u0440\u0435\u0439 \u043f\u0440\u043e\u0438\u0437\u043d\u043e\u0441\u0438\u0442 \u0437\u0430 \u0432\u0441\u044e \u0436\u0438\u0437\u043d\u044c! \u041e\u0431\u044b\u0447\u043d\u043e \u043f\u0435\u0440\u0432\u043e\u0435, \u0447\u0442\u043e \u0443\u0447\u0438\u0442 \u0435\u0432\u0440\u0435\u0439\u0441\u043a\u0438\u0439 \u0440\u0435\u0431\u0451\u043d\u043e\u043a, \u0438 \u0447\u0430\u0441\u0442\u043e \u043f\u043e\u0441\u043b\u0435\u0434\u043d\u0438\u0435 \u0441\u043b\u043e\u0432\u0430 \u043f\u0435\u0440\u0435\u0434 \u0443\u0445\u043e\u0434\u043e\u043c. \u041c\u044b \u0447\u0438\u0442\u0430\u0435\u043c \u0435\u0433\u043e \u0434\u0432\u0430\u0436\u0434\u044b \u0432 \u0434\u0435\u043d\u044c (\u0443\u0442\u0440\u043e\u043c \u0438 \u0432\u0435\u0447\u0435\u0440\u043e\u043c) \u043a\u0430\u043a \u0437\u0430\u043f\u043e\u0432\u0435\u0434\u044c \u0422\u043e\u0440\u044b. #16 cloud16 — Practice Hitbodedut — talk to Hashem in your own words

EN Practice Hitbodedut \u2014 talk to Hashem in your own words! \ud83c\udf33 Did you know Rabbi Nachman of Breslov taught that this is among the 'highest levels' of prayer? Hitbodedut is setting aside dedicated time (ideally in a quiet, private place like a field or forest, or even just your room!) to speak intimately with Hashem, just like you would with your best friend. Pour out your heart in your native language about anything and everything \u2013 your worries, dreams, gratitude, questions, or just your day. Rabbi Nachman emphasized that this unscripted, spontaneous prayer 'rises to a very high place' and creates tremendous spiritual delight and connection. Even 5-10 minutes a day can transform your spiritual life! Source: Likutei Moharan II, 25; Rabbi Nachman's Teachings.
HE \u05ea\u05e8\u05d2\u05dc\u05d5 \u05d4\u05ea\u05d1\u05d5\u05d3\u05d3\u05d5\u05ea \u2014 \u05d3\u05d1\u05e8\u05d5 \u05e2\u05dd \u05d4' \u05d1\u05de\u05d9\u05dc\u05d9\u05dd \u05e9\u05dc\u05db\u05dd! \ud83c\udf33 \u05d9\u05d3\u05e2\u05ea\u05dd \u05e9\u05e8\u05d1\u05d9 \u05e0\u05d7\u05de\u05df \u05de\u05d1\u05e8\u05e1\u05dc\u05d1 \u05dc\u05d9\u05de\u05d3 \u05e9\u05d6\u05d5 \u05d1\u05d9\u05df \"\u05d4\u05e8\u05de\u05d5\u05ea \u05d4\u05d2\u05d1\u05d5\u05d4\u05d5\u05ea \u05d1\u05d9\u05d5\u05ea\u05e8\" \u05e9\u05dc \u05ea\u05e4\u05d9\u05dc\u05d4? \u05d4\u05ea\u05d1\u05d5\u05d3\u05d3\u05d5\u05ea \u05d4\u05d9\u05d0 \u05dc\u05d4\u05e7\u05d3\u05d9\u05e9 \u05d6\u05de\u05df (\u05d1\u05de\u05e7\u05d5\u05dd \u05e9\u05e7\u05d8 \u05d5\u05e4\u05e8\u05d8\u05d9 \u2014 \u05e9\u05d3\u05d4, \u05d9\u05e2\u05e8, \u05d0\u05d5 \u05d0\u05e4\u05d9\u05dc\u05d5 \u05d4\u05d7\u05d3\u05e8 \u05e9\u05dc\u05db\u05dd!) \u05dc\u05d3\u05d1\u05e8 \u05d0\u05d9\u05e0\u05d8\u05d9\u05de\u05d9 \u05e2\u05dd \u05d4', \u05db\u05de\u05d5 \u05e2\u05dd \u05d7\u05d1\u05e8 \u05d4\u05db\u05d9 \u05d8\u05d5\u05d1. \u05e9\u05e4\u05db\u05d5 \u05d0\u05ea \u05dc\u05d1\u05db\u05dd \u05d1\u05e9\u05e4\u05ea \u05d0\u05dd \u05e2\u05dc \u05db\u05dc \u05d3\u05d1\u05e8 \u2014 \u05d3\u05d0\u05d2\u05d5\u05ea, \u05d7\u05dc\u05d5\u05de\u05d5\u05ea, \u05d4\u05db\u05e8\u05ea \u05ea\u05d5\u05d3\u05d4, \u05e9\u05d0\u05dc\u05d5\u05ea, \u05d0\u05d5 \u05e1\u05ea\u05dd \u05d4\u05d9\u05d5\u05dd \u05e9\u05dc\u05db\u05dd. \u05e8\u05d1\u05d9 \u05e0\u05d7\u05de\u05df \u05d4\u05d3\u05d2\u05d9\u05e9 \u05e9\u05ea\u05e4\u05d9\u05dc\u05d4 \u05e1\u05e4\u05d5\u05e0\u05d8\u05e0\u05d9\u05ea \u05d5\u05dc\u05d0 \u05db\u05ea\u05d5\u05d1\u05d4 \"\u05e2\u05d5\u05dc\u05d4 \u05dc\u05de\u05e7\u05d5\u05dd \u05d2\u05d1\u05d5\u05d4 \u05de\u05d0\u05d5\u05d3\" \u05d5\u05d9\u05d5\u05e6\u05e8\u05ea \u05e2\u05d5\u05e0\u05d2 \u05e8\u05d5\u05d7\u05e0\u05d9 \u05d5\u05e7\u05e9\u05e8 \u05e2\u05e6\u05d5\u05dd. \u05d0\u05e4\u05d9\u05dc\u05d5 5\u201310 \u05d3\u05e7\u05d5\u05ea \u05d1\u05d9\u05d5\u05dd \u05d9\u05db\u05d5\u05dc\u05d5\u05ea \u05dc\u05e9\u05e0\u05d5\u05ea \u05d0\u05ea \u05d4\u05d7\u05d9\u05d9\u05dd \u05d4\u05e8\u05d5\u05d7\u05e0\u05d9\u05d9\u05dd! \u05de\u05e7\u05d5\u05e8: \u05dc\u05d9\u05e7\u05d5\u05d8\u05d9 \u05de\u05d5\u05d4\u05e8\"\u05df \u05d7\u05dc\u05e7 \u05d1, \u05db\"\u05d4; \u05ea\u05d5\u05e8\u05d5\u05ea \u05e8\u05d1\u05d9 \u05e0\u05d7\u05de\u05df.
ES \u00a1Practica hitbodedut \u2014 habla con Hashem con tus propias palabras! \ud83c\udf33 \u00bfSab\u00edas que el rab\u00ed Najm\u00e1n de Breslov ense\u00f1\u00f3 que esto est\u00e1 entre los \"niveles m\u00e1s altos\" de oraci\u00f3n? Hitbodedut es reservar tiempo (idealmente en un lugar tranquilo y privado \u2014 un campo, un bosque, \u00a1o tu habitaci\u00f3n!) para hablar \u00edntimamente con Hashem, como con tu mejor amigo. Derrama tu coraz\u00f3n en tu idioma sobre todo \u2014 preocupaciones, sue\u00f1os, gratitud, preguntas o simplemente tu d\u00eda. El rab\u00ed Najm\u00e1n enfatiz\u00f3 que esta oraci\u00f3n espont\u00e1nea \"asciende a un lugar muy alto\" y crea enorme deleite espiritual. \u00a1Incluso 5-10 minutos al d\u00eda pueden transformar tu vida espiritual! Fuente: Likut\u00e9 Mohar\u00e1n II, 25; Ense\u00f1anzas del rab\u00ed Najm\u00e1n.
FR Pratiquez le hitbodedout \u2014 parlez \u00e0 D. avec vos propres mots ! \ud83c\udf33 Saviez-vous que Rabbi Nahman de Breslev enseignait que c'est parmi les \u00ab plus hauts niveaux \u00bb de pri\u00e8re ? Le hitbodedout, c'est r\u00e9server du temps (id\u00e9alement dans un endroit calme et priv\u00e9 \u2014 un champ, une for\u00eat, ou m\u00eame votre chambre !) pour parler intimement avec D., comme avec votre meilleur ami. D\u00e9versez votre c\u0153ur dans votre langue sur tout \u2014 soucis, r\u00eaves, gratitude, questions ou simplement votre journ\u00e9e. Rabbi Nahman soulignait que cette pri\u00e8re spontan\u00e9e \u00ab monte tr\u00e8s haut \u00bb et cr\u00e9e un immense d\u00e9lice spirituel. M\u00eame 5 \u00e0 10 minutes par jour peuvent transformer votre vie spirituelle ! Source : Likout\u00e9 Moharan II, 25 ; Enseignements de Rabbi Nahman.

#17 cloud17 — Uncover the good point — practice Azamra

EN Uncover the good point \u2014 practice Azamra! \ud83c\udfb5 This is one of Rabbi Nachman of Breslov's most transformative teachings: even in a person who seems completely lost or flawed, you *must* search until you find a single spark of goodness within them. By focusing on that good point, judging them favorably, you can actually help elevate both them and yourself spiritually! 'Azamra' means 'I will sing,' because by finding and celebrating that hidden good, you create a melody of praise to Hashem. Try this powerful exercise today: pick someone (or even look within yourself!) and consciously identify one genuinely positive quality. Watch how this shift in perspective can transform your entire outlook! Source: Likutei Moharan I, 282; Rabbi Nachman's Teachings.

ES \u00a1Descubre el punto bueno \u2014 practica Azamr\u00e1! \ud83c\udfb5 Esta es una de las ense\u00f1anzas m\u00e1s transformadoras del rab\u00ed Najm\u00e1n: incluso en alguien que parece completamente perdido o defectuoso, debes buscar hasta encontrar una sola chispa de bondad. Prueba hoy: elige a alguien (\u00a1o m\u00edrate a ti mismo!) e identifica una cualidad genuinamente positiva. \u00a1Observa c\u00f3mo este cambio de perspectiva transforma tu visi\u00f3n! FR D\u00e9couvrez le bon point \u2014 pratiquez Azamra ! \ud83c\udfb5 C'est l'un des enseignements les plus transformateurs de Rabbi Nahman : m\u00eame chez une personne qui semble totalement perdue ou d\u00e9faillante, vous devez chercher jusqu'\u00e0 trouver une seule \u00e9tincelle de bont\u00e9. Source : Likout\u00e9 Moharan I, 282 ; Enseignements de Rabbi Nahman.

#18 cloud18 — Serve Hashem with Simcha (Joy)

EN Serve Hashem with Simcha (Joy)! \ud83d\ude0a This isn't just a nice idea; Rabbi Nachman of Breslov (Likutei Moharan I, 24) teaches that performing mitzvot with joy elevates them to the highest spiritual levels, connecting them to the Keter (the 'crown' of creation)! He emphasized that joy is the key to spiritual breakthroughs and moving forward in life when you feel stuck. Think of it: a mitzvah done with a smile, song, or even a little dance is far more impactful! Your mission today: choose one mitzvah and perform it with extra happiness \u2013 whether it's giving tzedakah with a cheerful heart, singing during Torah study, or truly celebrating after prayer. Rabbi Nachman taught that joy isn't optional; it's how we access profound spiritual growth and closeness to Hashem! Source: Likutei Moharan I, 24; Rabbi Nachman's Teachings.

ES \u00a1Sirve a Hashem con simj\u00e1 (alegr\u00eda)! \ud83d\ude0a No es solo una buena idea: el rab\u00ed Najm\u00e1n (Likut\u00e9 Mohar\u00e1n I, 24) ense\u00f1a que cumplir mitzvot con alegr\u00eda las eleva a los niveles espirituales m\u00e1s altos, conect\u00e1ndolas al Keter (la \"corona\" de la creaci\u00f3n). Tu misi\u00f3n hoy: elige una mitzv\u00e1 y hazla con felicidad extra \u2014 ya sea dar tzedak\u00e1 con coraz\u00f3n alegre, cantar durante el estudio de Tor\u00e1 o celebrar de verdad despu\u00e9s de orar. El rab\u00ed Najm\u00e1n ense\u00f1\u00f3 que la alegr\u00eda no es opcional: \u00a1es c\u00f3mo accedemos al crecimiento espiritual profundo! Fuente: Likut\u00e9 Mohar\u00e1n I, 24; Ense\u00f1anzas del rab\u00ed Najm\u00e1n.
FR Servez D. avec la sim'ha (joie) ! \ud83d\ude0a Ce n'est pas qu'une bonne id\u00e9e : Rabbi Nahman (Likout\u00e9 Moharan I, 24) enseigne qu'accomplir des mitzvot avec joie les \u00e9l\u00e8ve aux plus hauts niveaux spirituels, les connectant au Keter (la \u00ab couronne \u00bb de la cr\u00e9ation) ! Il soulignait que la joie est la cl\u00e9 des perc\u00e9es spirituelles quand on se sent bloqu\u00e9. Une mitzvah faite avec un sourire, une chanson ou une petite danse est bien plus impactante ! Votre mission aujourd'hui : choisissez une mitzvah et accomplissez-la avec une joie extra \u2014 que ce soit donner de la tsedaka avec un c\u0153ur l\u00e9ger, chanter pendant l'\u00e9tude de la Torah ou vraiment c\u00e9l\u00e9brer apr\u00e8s la pri\u00e8re. Rabbi Nahman enseignait que la joie n'est pas optionnelle \u2014 c'est ainsi qu'on acc\u00e8de \u00e0 une croissance spirituelle profonde ! Source : Likout\u00e9 Moharan I, 24 ; Enseignements de Rabbi Nahman.

#19 cloud19 — Remember this powerful truth: There is absolutely NO despair in the world

EN Remember this powerful truth: There is absolutely NO despair in the world! \ud83d\udcaa Rabbi Nachman of Breslov's most famous declaration \u2014 'Ein shum ye'ush ba'olam klal!' \u2014 is a game-changer. It means that no matter how far someone feels they've fallen, no matter how many mistakes they've made, return to Hashem is always possible. Every challenge has a solution, every misstep can be rectified, and spiritual renewal is always just a moment away. When discouragement strikes, repeat this phrase aloud in Hebrew or English and let it infuse you with strength and hope. Rabbi Nachman based this on deep Kabbalistic insights: despair presumes your situation is permanent, but that fundamentally misunderstands the fluid, dynamic reality of Divine mercy. Redemption can literally happen in the blink of an eye! Source: Likutei Moharan II, 78; Rabbi Nachman's Teachings.

#20 cloud20 — Discover the Tikkun HaKlali — Rabbi Nachman's powerful ten psalms

EN Discover the Tikkun HaKlali \u2014 Rabbi Nachman's powerful ten psalms! \ud83d\udcd6 Rabbi Nachman of Breslov revealed a specific spiritual remedy known as the Tikkun HaKlali (General Rectification), consisting of ten chapters of Tehillim (Psalms 16, 32, 41, 42, 59, 77, 90, 105, 137, 150). He taught that this special collection has immense power to rectify the soul, particularly in cases of spiritual impurity or distress. What's truly remarkable? Rabbi Nachman stated that the revelation of this unique remedy was 'a very wonderful and awesome rectification' that had remained hidden since the time of Creation! You can recite these psalms anytime you need spiritual cleansing, strength, or a profound connection to Hashem. Source: Likutei Moharan I, 205; Rabbi Nachman's Teachings.

#21 cloud21 — Supercharge your prayers with Tzedakah (Charity)

EN Supercharge your prayers with Tzedakah (Charity)! \ud83d\udcb0 It's a powerful tradition, taught by great sages, to give charity *before* prayer and Torah study. Why? Giving tzedakah opens the 'gates of compassion' in Heaven and elevates your spiritual endeavors! Rabbi Nachman connected tzedakah to mystical light, explaining that every act of giving, even a small coin with a sincere heart, creates a channel for Divine illumination to flow into the world. It\u2019s like preparing the ground for your spiritual seeds to grow! Before your next prayer session or learning, try dropping a coin into a tzedakah box (or giving online) and notice how it deepens your connection to Hashem. Source: Talmud, Bava Batra 10a; Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim 92:1; Rabbi Nachman's Teachings.

ES \u00a1Potencia tus oraciones con tzedak\u00e1 (caridad)! \ud83d\udcb0 Es una poderosa tradici\u00f3n, ense\u00f1ada por grandes sabios, dar caridad antes de la oraci\u00f3n y el estudio de Tor\u00e1. \u00bfPor qu\u00e9? Dar tzedak\u00e1 abre las \"puertas de la compasi\u00f3n\" en el Cielo y eleva tus esfuerzos espirituales. El rab\u00ed Najm\u00e1n conect\u00f3 la tzedak\u00e1 con la luz m\u00edstica, explicando que cada acto de dar, incluso una moneda peque\u00f1a con coraz\u00f3n sincero, crea un canal para que la iluminaci\u00f3n divina fluya al mundo. \u00a1Es como preparar la tierra para que crezcan tus semillas espirituales! Antes de tu pr\u00f3xima sesi\u00f3n de oraci\u00f3n o estudio, intenta poner una moneda en una caja de tzedak\u00e1 (o donar en l\u00ednea) y nota c\u00f3mo profundiza tu conexi\u00f3n con Hashem. Fuente: Talmud, Bava Batra 10a; Shulj\u00e1n Aruj, Oraj Jaim 92:1; Ense\u00f1anzas del rab\u00ed Najm\u00e1n.
FR Boostez vos pri\u00e8res avec la tsedaka (charit\u00e9) ! \ud83d\udcb0 C'est une puissante tradition, enseign\u00e9e par de grands sages, de donner la charit\u00e9 avant la pri\u00e8re et l'\u00e9tude de la Torah. Pourquoi ? Donner la tsedaka ouvre les \u00ab portes de la compassion \u00bb au Ciel et \u00e9l\u00e8ve vos efforts spirituels ! Rabbi Nahman reliait la tsedaka \u00e0 la lumi\u00e8re mystique, expliquant que chaque acte de don, m\u00eame une petite pi\u00e8ce avec un c\u0153ur sinc\u00e8re, cr\u00e9e un canal pour que l'illumination divine coule dans le monde. C'est comme pr\u00e9parer le sol pour que vos graines spirituelles poussent ! Avant votre prochaine session de pri\u00e8re ou d'\u00e9tude, essayez de mettre une pi\u00e8ce dans une bo\u00eete de tsedaka (ou de donner en ligne) et notez comment cela approfondit votre connexion \u00e0 D. Source : Talmud, Bava Batra 10a ; Choulhan Aroukh, Ora'h 'Ha\u00efm 92:1 ; Enseignements de Rabbi Nahman.

#22 cloud22 — Level up your character: Study Pirkei Avot

EN Level up your character: Study Pirkei Avot! \ud83d\udcda Pirkei Avot, the 'Ethics of the Fathers,' is a treasure trove of timeless wisdom for daily life and middot (character development). Each short teaching offers profound, practical guidance on how to be a truly good person, treat others with kindness and integrity, and serve Hashem with humility and intention. These aren't just ancient sayings; they are foundational Jewish values that have shaped our ethical framework for over 2,000 years! Make it a weekly habit: pick your favorite lesson from any chapter and reflect on how you can apply its wisdom to your own life today. It's a spiritual workout for your soul! Source: Mishnah, Pirkei Avot; Talmud, Bava Kama 30a (regarding the importance of ethical conduct).

Cada ense\u00f1anza corta ofrece gu\u00eda pr\u00e1ctica y profunda sobre c\u00f3mo ser una buena persona, tratar a otros con bondad e integridad, y servir a Hashem con humildad e intenci\u00f3n. \u00a1No son solo dichos antiguos: son valores jud\u00edos fundamentales que han moldeado nuestro marco \u00e9tico por m\u00e1s de 2,000 a\u00f1os! FR Am\u00e9liorez votre caract\u00e8re : \u00e9tudiez Pirk\u00e9 Avot ! \ud83d\udcda Pirk\u00e9 Avot, l'\u00ab \u00c9thique des P\u00e8res \u00bb, est un tr\u00e9sor de sagesse intemporelle pour la vie quotidienne et les middot (d\u00e9veloppement du caract\u00e8re). Chaque court enseignement offre des conseils pratiques et profonds sur comment \u00eatre une bonne personne, traiter les autres avec bont\u00e9 et int\u00e9grit\u00e9, et servir D. avec humilit\u00e9 et intention. Ce ne sont pas que des maximes anciennes : ce sont des valeurs juives fondamentales qui ont fa\u00e7onn\u00e9 notre cadre \u00e9thique depuis plus de 2 000 ans ! Faites-en une habitude hebdomadaire : choisissez votre le\u00e7on favorite de n'importe quel chapitre et r\u00e9fl\u00e9chissez \u00e0 comment appliquer sa sagesse aujourd'hui. C'est un entra\u00eenement spirituel pour l'\u00e2me ! Source : Mishna, Pirk\u00e9 Avot ; Talmud, Bava Kama 30a.

#23 cloud23 — Transform your worries into prayers

EN Transform your worries into prayers! \ud83d\udd4a\ufe0f Rabbi Nachman of Breslov taught a revolutionary approach to anxiety: instead of letting worried thoughts spiral, *transform* them into heartfelt conversations with Hashem through Hitbodedut! Whatever is bothering you \u2013 big or small, trivial or overwhelming \u2013 speak to G-d about it in your own words, out loud if possible. This powerful practice takes negative, draining energy and redirects it toward spiritual growth, profound trust, and a deeper connection to the Divine. Try it right now: pick one worry that's on your mind and talk it through with Hashem. You'll be amazed at the clarity and peace it brings! Source: Likutei Moharan II, 25; Rabbi Nachman's Teachings.

#24 cloud24 — Elevate your day: Express gratitude out loud to Hashem

EN Elevate your day: Express gratitude out loud to Hashem! \ud83d\ude4f Rabbi Nachman of Breslov and countless sages teach that actively thanking Hashem for *everything* \u2013 even challenges \u2013 is a profound spiritual practice. It transforms harsh judgments into mercy and opens spiritual gates to blessings! Right now, try saying 'Thank You, Hashem!' for three *specific* things in your life. Be detailed: instead of a general 'thanks for food,' try 'Thank You, Hashem, for the delicious and nourishing breakfast I had this morning that gave me energy, and for all the amazing flavors infused in it!' Speaking your gratitude aloud creates a powerful spiritual channel and shifts your entire perspective. Source: Likutei Moharan I, 79; Rabbi Nachman's Teachings.

#25 cloud25 — Level up your day: Learn one halacha (Jewish law) daily

EN Level up your day: Learn one halacha (Jewish law) daily! \ud83d\udcda The Sages teach that consistent Torah learning \u2013 even just one practical halacha a day \u2013 is a powerful way to stay connected to Hashem and His profound wisdom throughout your life. It's like a daily spiritual vitamin! Pick a topic that sparks your curiosity: Shabbat laws, the intricate blessings on food, business ethics, Kashrut, or how to treat others with respect. Whether it's from a Mishnah, Gemara, Shulchan Aruch, or a contemporary sefer, small, steady learning builds an unshakable foundation for a meaningful Jewish life. Did you know? Daily Torah study, particularly of halacha, is considered one of the acts that 'has no measure' \u2013 meaning its spiritual reward is truly infinite!
HE \u05e9\u05d3\u05e8\u05d2\u05d5 \u05d0\u05ea \u05d4\u05d9\u05d5\u05dd: \u05dc\u05de\u05d3\u05d5 \u05d4\u05dc\u05db\u05d4 \u05d0\u05d7\u05ea \u05d1\u05d9\u05d5\u05dd! \ud83d\udcda \u05d4\u05d7\u05db\u05de\u05d9\u05dd \u05de\u05dc\u05de\u05d3\u05d9\u05dd \u05e9\u05dc\u05d9\u05de\u05d5\u05d3 \u05ea\u05d5\u05e8\u05d4 \u05e2\u05e7\u05d1\u05d9 \u2014 \u05d0\u05e4\u05d9\u05dc\u05d5 \u05d4\u05dc\u05db\u05d4 \u05de\u05e2\u05e9\u05d9\u05ea \u05d0\u05d7\u05ea \u05d1\u05d9\u05d5\u05dd \u2014 \u05d4\u05d5\u05d0 \u05d3\u05e8\u05da \u05e2\u05d5\u05e6\u05de\u05ea\u05d9\u05ea \u05dc\u05d4\u05d9\u05e9\u05d0\u05e8 \u05de\u05d7\u05d5\u05d1\u05e8\u05d9\u05dd \u05dc\u05d4' \u05d5\u05dc\u05d7\u05db\u05de\u05ea\u05d5 \u05dc\u05d0\u05d5\u05e8\u05da \u05d4\u05d7\u05d9\u05d9\u05dd. \u05d6\u05d4 \u05db\u05de\u05d5 \u05d5\u05d9\u05d8\u05de\u05d9\u05df \u05e8\u05d5\u05d7\u05e0\u05d9 \u05d9\u05d5\u05de\u05d9! \u05d1\u05d7\u05e8\u05d5 \u05e0\u05d5\u05e9\u05d0 \u05e9\u05de\u05e2\u05d5\u05e8\u05e8 \u05e1\u05e7\u05e8\u05e0\u05d5\u05ea: \u05d4\u05dc\u05db\u05d5\u05ea \u05e9\u05d1\u05ea, \u05d1\u05e8\u05db\u05d5\u05ea \u05e2\u05dc \u05de\u05d0\u05db\u05dc\u05d9\u05dd, \u05d0\u05ea\u05d9\u05e7\u05d4 \u05d1\u05e2\u05e1\u05e7\u05d9\u05dd, \u05db\u05e9\u05e8\u05d5\u05ea, \u05d0\u05d5 \u05db\u05d1\u05d5\u05d3 \u05d4\u05d1\u05e8\u05d9\u05d5\u05ea. \u05d1\u05d9\u05df \u05d0\u05dd \u05de\u05de\u05e9\u05e0\u05d4, \u05d2\u05de\u05e8\u05d0, \u05e9\u05d5\u05dc\u05d7\u05df \u05e2\u05e8\u05d5\u05da \u05d0\u05d5 \u05e1\u05e4\u05e8 \u05e2\u05db\u05e9\u05d5\u05d5\u05d9 \u2014 \u05dc\u05d9\u05de\u05d5\u05d3 \u05e7\u05d8\u05df \u05d5\u05e7\u05d1\u05d5\u05e2 \u05d1\u05d5\u05e0\u05d4 \u05d9\u05e1\u05d5\u05d3 \u05d1\u05dc\u05ea\u05d9 \u05e0\u05d9\u05ea\u05df \u05dc\u05e2\u05e8\u05e2\u05d5\u05e8 \u05dc\u05d7\u05d9\u05d9\u05dd \u05d9\u05d4\u05d5\u05d3\u05d9\u05d9\u05dd \u05de\u05e9\u05de\u05e2\u05d5\u05ea\u05d9\u05d9\u05dd. \u05d9\u05d3\u05e2\u05ea\u05dd? ES Eleva tu d\u00eda: \u00a1aprende una halaj\u00e1 (ley jud\u00eda) diaria! \ud83d\udcda Los Sabios ense\u00f1an que el estudio constante de Tor\u00e1 \u2014 incluso solo una halaj\u00e1 pr\u00e1ctica al d\u00eda \u2014 es una forma poderosa de mantenerse conectado a Hashem y a Su sabidur\u00eda a lo largo de la vida. \u00a1Es como una vitamina espiritual diaria! Elige un tema que despierte tu curiosidad: leyes de Shabat, bendiciones sobre alimentos, \u00e9tica empresarial, kashrut o c\u00f3mo tratar a otros con respeto. Ya sea de la Mishn\u00e1, el Guemar\u00e1, el Shulj\u00e1n Aruj o un sefer contempor\u00e1neo, el aprendizaje peque\u00f1o y constante construye una base inquebrantable para una vida jud\u00eda significativa. \u00bfSab\u00edas? El estudio diario de Tor\u00e1, especialmente de halaj\u00e1, se considera una de las acciones que \"no tienen medida\" \u2014 \u00a1su recompensa espiritual es verdaderamente infinita!
FR \u00c9levez votre journ\u00e9e : apprenez une halacha (loi juive) par jour ! \ud83d\udcda Les Sages enseignent qu'une \u00e9tude constante de la Torah \u2014 m\u00eame une seule halacha pratique par jour \u2014 est un moyen puissant de rester connect\u00e9 \u00e0 D. et \u00e0 Sa sagesse tout au long de la vie. C'est comme une vitamine spirituelle quotidienne ! Choisissez un sujet qui \u00e9veille votre curiosit\u00e9 : lois du Chabbat, b\u00e9n\u00e9dictions sur les aliments, \u00e9thique des affaires, cacherout ou comment traiter les autres avec respect. Que ce soit dans la Mishna, le Gu\u00e9mara, le Choulhan Aroukh ou un sefer contemporain, un apprentissage petit et r\u00e9gulier construit une base in\u00e9branlable pour une vie juive significative. Le saviez-vous ? L'\u00e9tude quotidienne de la Torah, surtout de la halacha, est consid\u00e9r\u00e9e comme l'une des actions qui \u00ab n'ont pas de mesure \u00bb \u2014 leur r\u00e9compense spirituelle est vraiment infinie !
